  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6988d769-622d-4961-912b-f420ec0cedfd'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer13653039335186052826">With her thirtieth birthday looming, Emma Harrison finds her biological clock clanging and the elusive knight in shining armor yet to appear. She’s running out of options, especially after her gay best friend backs out from being her sperm donor.   <span id="freeText13653039335186052826" style="display:none">With her thirtieth birthday looming, Emma Harrison finds her biological clock clanging and the elusive knight in shining armor yet to appear. She’s running out of options, especially after her gay best friend backs out from being her sperm donor. Of course, there’s always a sperm bank, but Emma fears a donor mix-up might impregnate her with the spawn of Satan.<br /><br />Resident company womanizer, Aidan Fitzgerald, is used to always getting what he wants, especially in the bedroom. When Emma spurns his advances at the company Christmas party, he's determined to have her no matter what it takes. After Aidan learns of Emma's predicament, he is quick to offer a proposition that will benefit them both. He will father Emma's child, but she must conceive it with him naturally. Not one for hook-ups or casual sex, Emma is reluctant to take him up on his offer, but his charm, coupled with her intense desire for motherhood, wins out.<br /> <br />Soon their baby-making sessions become more than just physical. Aidan can't seem to walk away from her while Emma begins to wonder if Aidan could be the one. But can Aidan leave his past behind to become the man Emma needs him to be?</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1700508698" />
    <a title="V.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1700508698?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="V. A Court of Wings and Ruin is NEW ADULT/EROTICA but Goodreads editors won&#39;t tell you to include it in the choice awards" class="user" itemprop="url" name="V. A Court of Wings and Ruin is NEW ADULT/EROTICA but Goodreads editors won&#39;t tell you to include it in the choice awards" href="/user/show/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors">V. A Court of Wings and Ruin is NEW ADULT/EROTICA but Goodreads editors won&#39;t tell you to include it in the choice awards</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=weak-hero">weak-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=pleasegrowupman">pleasegrowupman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=heroisaboypretendingtobeaman">heroisaboypretendingtobeaman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=antifeminist">antifeminist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=separation-cuz-unnesessary-drama">separation-cuz-unnesessary-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=mysoginist">mysoginist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=disloyal-hero">disloyal-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=cheating-hero">cheating-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1700508698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8069208807266766585"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471135791ra/20005222.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Grrrr! I'm so angry. Another one to cheating shelf. Or in this case disloyal, weak hero wants to hurt the person he claims he loves. <b>Careful with this one my safety gang!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471135791ra/20005223.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm so upset that I wasted time on this book. It was free and I asked a friend from a smut reads club if there was cheating in this book and she told me no. That's why I read it. It's not like my club-friend lied to me, it's just that I'm extremely sensitive to disloyalty and weakness and most romance readers aren't. "Technical</span>
  <span id="freeText8069208807266766585" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471135791ra/20005222.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Grrrr! I'm so angry. Another one to cheating shelf. Or in this case disloyal, weak hero wants to hurt the person he claims he loves. <b>Careful with this one my safety gang!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471135791ra/20005223.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm so upset that I wasted time on this book. It was free and I asked a friend from a smut reads club if there was cheating in this book and she told me no. That's why I read it. It's not like my club-friend lied to me, it's just that I'm extremely sensitive to disloyalty and weakness and most romance readers aren't. "Technically" Aidan the hero <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["did not have sexual relationships with that woman"  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>*sighs<br><br>As I said in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610640521" rel="nofollow noopener"> Paper Princess review</a>: <b>After hero and heroine have kissed any kind of physical contact with another woman is 100% unacceptable. </b> That only makes the hero weak and flickery and speaks volumes of the lack of ability of a huge majority of self-published erotica authors to create drama that doesn't involve a separation from the couple.<br><br><br>UPCOMING RANT!<br><br>You must know that I became addicted to romance when I discovered the twilight books in my eleventh birthday. I was 15 when I read Master of the Universe nowadays known as FSOG and later I fell in love with Gideon Cross from the Crossfire series and Travis Maddox from Beautiful disaster. Yes, I know that these books portray manipulative, unhealthy relationships that in real life would have ended in restraining orders, divorce, and physical violence, IN THE FICTIONAL REALM thESE couples work. Imperfect, flawed, stalkery people fall in love too and usually a good hero changes for / with the love of the heroine and we get our happy endings as we should.<br><br><br>But how the hell would Katie Ashley fix this mess in the sequel of this train-wreck? Not after he treated her so badly. I didn't like Emma much, she was, as a huge bunch contemporary erotica heroines are, disgustingly agreeable to the point of weakness and a slut-shamer. But I at least could understand where she came from and was interested enough in seeing her succeed to end the story. Now, after that twist at the end, the sequels are ruined for me. If she forgives that kind of conduct she doesn't deserve to have a happy ending. Not after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the very pregnant heroine caught the father of her baby trying to fuck another woman, the very day he failed to be there with her for an ultrasound. The dog is more loyal than the hero.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br>Seriously self-published erotica authors, can't you think of another way to bring drama that doesn't involve cheating? Haven't you noticed that for all the shit they receive in goodreads Edward, Christian Grey and Gideon CroSs NEVER CHEATED, NEVER SLUTSHAMED OTHER WOMEN AND ONCE THEY MET THEIR HEROINES DIDN'T HAVE EYES FOR ANOTHER WOMAN? That's what makes them so likeable, that's why these books have cross-over appeal. CHEATING IS NOT ACCEPTABLE AND MAKES YOUR HERO UNLIKEABLE AND WEAK and overall FORGETTABLE. Thrown to the bad-bookboyfriends pile.<br><br>I don't care if they were on a break, in this case they weren't. I don't care if the hero has been <b>drugged, drunk, depressed, confused, weakened by a disease, abducted by aliens, imperiused, bewitched, tortured into submission, blackmailed, deceived or "trying to protect the heroine".</b> That's just stupid, unbelievable and again, if your hero can't fight against the urges of his dick (and if he's in love why would he have to have urges for another woman?) then he doesn't deserve the heroine. He doesn't even deserve to be called A MAN. He can go with the other boys pretending to be grown ups that abound in New adult/erotica fiction.<br><br>Let's get this straight. Romance is a genre that should be all about swooning, fangirling, laughing, having fun and finding unrealistic, strong, flawed, charming MEN; emphasis in men. I'm not into boys in romance unless they are super-mature and cute, (I'm looking at you Will Herondale), I'm into men that you wouldn't find in real life, or at least you wouldn't find them often. So what's the point of reading a "romance" book if the hero will act like any cliched TV Manwhore?<br><br> Slutshaming is starting to become a deal-breaker for me because it's becoming so cliche even if in the past I've rated 5 stars slutshame-fests like Beautiful disaster in which Abby slut-shames not only every female around, but also acts like Travis deserves to be punished for sleeping around, therefore slutshaming him too. <b>Slut-shaming is a form of discrimination not different than homophobia. All people should be treated equally and with respect disregarding, creed, fashion choices, race, economical status, physical apperance, and sexual decisions .</b> A woman's or man's worth is not based on how many times or with whom they have sex. Sex isn't a sin, sex is not a taboo and people who sleeps around could be as moral and worthy as people who don't. But see? In Beautiful disaster both Abby and Travis are young, they are in their school years so they can grow up into open-minded people who don't slut shame and anyway Travis is just adorable (although he also almost cheated, but they were on a "real", we'll-never-ever-ever -be-back-together separation. In this book the couple is supposedly near their thirties so why they don't have more maturity than plenty of YA, even middle-grade books couples?<br><br>I honestly should stick to classic romance written by authors that have been writing romance for decades (case in point Susan Elizabeth Philips or Lisa Kleypas) or good New adult authors like Colleen Hoover. "Adult" erotica is full of immature MC's. I think I might give up the adult (characters over 22) self-published contemporary romance for good. I just end up pissed-off and having no fun from those reads. I want to read a good steamy romance in which adults act like adults. <i>Update October 8th. I was just being dramatic. I found a good New adult/Erotica read called The deal by Elle Kennedy and a couple of short stories that made me remember that comtemporary erotica is fun when it's well done.</i><br><br>Now, I think that the first sex scenes of this book are good and steamy, and anyone who doesn't mind slutshaming, separated couple, disloyal hero, adults acting like teens, might enjoy the book. Most romances on KU are like this one and still get good ratings so I'm perhaps too much into unrealistic heroes, to understand why this book has such high rating. So don't take me too seriously. The book is free so you might like it more than I did.<br> <br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8069208807266766585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440538640?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440538640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18218821254992090058"><b> I. NEED. BOOK. TWO. RIGHT. FREAKING. NOW. </b><br/><br/><img width='60%' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383653ra/741939.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Gah! Ok, so I knew there was a cliffhanger when I went into this book and early on in the book there is a big "hint" at what its about that I picked up on, so on all accounts, I was ready for it but <b> holy hell my heart was in knots by the end!!!! </b><br/><br/><i> *falls down on knees and begs Katie Ashley for an early release of The Proposal* </i><br/><br/>I have to say, the synopsis of this book was what grabbed me. The minute I read it, I just knew that I had to read this book!!<br/><br/>Wi</span>
  <span id="freeText18218821254992090058" style="display:none"><b> I. NEED. BOOK. TWO. RIGHT. FREAKING. NOW. </b><br><br><img width="60%" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383653ra/741939.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gah! Ok, so I knew there was a cliffhanger when I went into this book and early on in the book there is a big "hint" at what its about that I picked up on, so on all accounts, I was ready for it but <b> holy hell my heart was in knots by the end!!!! </b><br><br><i> *falls down on knees and begs Katie Ashley for an early release of The Proposal* </i><br><br>I have to say, the synopsis of this book was what grabbed me. The minute I read it, I just knew that I had to read this book!!<br><br>With her 30th birthday looming over her, Emma feels her biological ticking. Loudly. But unfortunately, there is no sign of Mr. Right anywhere even near the horizon. So she decided to give single motherhood a shot but when her gay best friend backs out of his promise to donate sperm to her cause, she is devastated.<br><br>And then in swoops her gorgeous, commitment phobic, serial womanizer, coworker Aidan with a proposition. *waggles eyebrows* He will father her child with the catch of it being conceived naturally.<br><br><i> "Look... Emma wanted the baby, so I agreed to help her."...<br>"Ah, you're like her stud horse or something?"<br>"Not funny." </i><br><br>And despite her early misgivings, Emma's desire for a child wins out and she takes him up on his offer.<br><br><i> <b> "A MWF sex schedule? How efficient," he mused.<br>"Please be serious."<br>A wicked grin flashed on his face. "Fine, pencil me in. I"ll be ready and erect whenever you need me." </b></i> <br><br>But Aidan was a man with serious commitment issues - who balked at any hint of being tied down to something permanent - no matter how much fullness it could bring to his life. And we are left to find out whether or not what he is beginning to feel for Emma will grow strong enough to overcome the man he is....<br><br><i> "...Aidan Fitzgerald is not husband material. But he's sure as hell stud material." </i><br><br>I really liked seeing these two people trying to take something so personal so seriously. And adorable watching their real feelings develop even while trying to maintain a "professional" (hmm, wrong word, but you know what I mean) attitude about the whole thing.<br><br>There were a few times where I found things a little rushed, and a moment or two that I wasn't sure about but overall, I just enjoyed the story.<br><br>Aidan... I kind of went back and forth on him. I started out grinning from ear to ear and loving where everything was going, totally looking forward to his character's growth and change and, especially once those started, my heart started to feel whole, but his commitment issues really tore at my heart and frustrated me.<br><br>At 90% I was ready to slap him.<br>At 94% I just wanted to throttle him.<br>At 95% I was ready to throw my kindle at him and tell him to go fuck himself.<br>At 96% I just wanted to hug Emma and geld him (and no, trust me, I'm not being too harsh, just read it, you'll want to do the same thing)<br><br>But..... then *holds up one finger* ... by 98% despite everything, I saw a spark that gave me hope for him being truly redeemable.<br><br>HOWEVER.....<br><br><b> Please please PLEASE may <i> The Proposal </i> have one of the most <u> epic freaking grovels </u> in book history!!!!!!!!!! </b><br><br>I love stories of characters who are able to catch themselves before they go too far, realize they are on the wrong path and do everything in their power to make things right again so I'm very, very, VERY much looking forward to book #2.<br><br>With MUCH. EPIC. GROVELING. (yes, its worth mentioning twice)<br><br>So yeah, you should know before you read it that the ending is a cliffhanger (clearly, lol)...<br>But. Big BUT here. --&gt; Its not the kind where it just ends in the middle of a scene, but rather just ends at a point where it gives you the feeling like things will be fixed in the end but right at the moment you finish, you'll be willing to barter your everloving soul for the sequel.<br><br>This book was a fun read. The story is not too long - I read it in one evening. There is humor, banter, a good plot (this book isn't just about the sex!) and leaves you desperate to see where the characters will end up.<br><br>And book 2, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16117804.The_Proposal__The_Proposition___2_" title="The Proposal (The Proposition, #2) by Katie Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Proposal</a>, has thankfully be bumped up to a January release instead of the original March by popular demand *wipes brow*<br><br><b> I.NEED. THAT. BOOK. </b><br><br>NOWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWW<br><br><img width="100%" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/612370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is all.<br><br>CASTING (these are Katie Ashley's choices):<br><br><a href="http://katieashleybooks.blogspot.ca/2012/10/the-propositions-main-players-or-excuse.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Click HERE for Katie Ashley's casting of her characters.</a><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395301i/761341._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img width="60%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395301i/761342.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>oh, and a big thank you to the author for sending me a copy &lt;3<br><br>For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18218821254992090058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_452695705" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452695705" />
    <a title="Baba  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669232-baba"><img alt="Baba  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564910043p2/4669232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452695705?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baba  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baba  " href="/user/show/4669232-baba">Baba  </a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16126502-the-proposition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669232-baba?shelf=rolls-eyes">rolls-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669232-baba?shelf=books-everyone-loved-but-baba">books-everyone-loved-but-baba</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669232-baba?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452695705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15629457872117807189"><b>DNF at 50 %. I will refrain from rating this book.</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1071.beta.photobucket.com/user/MsBaba4/library/gifs' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397150ra/766112.gif' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/> <br/>Although I was looking forward to reading <i>The Proposition,</i> I ended up disappointed once again. Sadly, the book could not live up to my high expectations.<br/> <br/><b>What did not work for me</b><br/>I was aware that <i>The Proposition</i> dealt with Em’s ticking biological clock. In addition, I was also aware of the fact that it was not quite believable. Yet I was sure that I could have dealt with it. Having said this, there are just too many issues that ruined the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText15629457872117807189" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 50 %. I will refrain from rating this book.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1071.beta.photobucket.com/user/MsBaba4/library/gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397150ra/766112.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>Although I was looking forward to reading <i>The Proposition,</i> I ended up disappointed once again. Sadly, the book could not live up to my high expectations.<br> <br><b>What did not work for me</b><br>I was aware that <i>The Proposition</i> dealt with Em’s ticking biological clock. In addition, I was also aware of the fact that it was not quite believable. Yet I was sure that I could have dealt with it. Having said this, there are just too many issues that ruined the book for me, though.<br><br>The beginning was very rushed, not really well developed. I love smexy times like every other reader but there was just plenty of <b>bland</b> sex that I was skimming pretty soon because I was bored. In fact, there was no chemistry, no sexual tension at all. That said, how can there be sexual tension or chemistry when you have scheduled sex? I mean there is nothing thrilling about that. Then again, it could have been very exciting if it would have been written differently. After all, some authors have the ability to write great chemistry <b>ad libitum.</b><br> <br>Aidan comes across as immature, rather shallow and boring. It goes without saying that he wants to get into Em’s pants as soon as possible. His jokes may have been entertaining now and then, but too many times they were simply cheap, cheesy and insensitive. An example:<br> <br><i>„I bet she spoiled you rotten,” Emma mused.<br>“She did and my four sisters.” He shook his head. “Jesus, it’s a wonder I’m not gay growing up around all that estrogen.”</i><br> <br>WTF? That’s not funny. What a heedless moron.<br> <br>Emma is <b>inconsiderate, weepy, whiny, overly melodramatic, and selfish.</b> Wanting to make up for sadness and disappointment in her life by getting pregnant sounds pretty darn selfish and shallow if you ask me. And I didn’t count how many times Em had tears in her eyes, was sobbing, crying, weeping, whining or…whatever.<br> <br><i>Aidan opened his mouth, but Emma kept barreling on, her voice raising an octave. “Or what if I just have this huge mental block that becomes a physical one where I can’t conceive? What if I wasted all my fertile years and now I’m just going to be barren and alone for the rest of my life?”</i><br> <br><b>After the first failed attempt</b> at getting pregnant she has a major breakdown and is sobbing and blabbering dumb stuff like that?? Granted, it’s also the two year anniversary of her mother passing away. <b>But.</b> I don’t get it why she had to freak out like that. After all, she is not even thirty yet. What about all those (married) couples who are trying very hard to conceive for years? And what about all those (married) couples who conceive multiple times and lose the embryo (or baby) time and again? <b>Em’s behavior has to feel like a slap to their face!</b> Incredible. What a drama queen.<br> <br>Emma finds kitchen counters offensive for conceiving. *scratches head* This woman would seriously kill my mood. :/<br> <br><i>Emma tossed her bag on the floorboard and then slid across the leather seat. Besides the fact it cost twice as much as her Honda, it was impeccably clean on the inside. Not a crumb or spec of dust could be found while in her car a small village could have been fed by leftover food of grabbing breakfast or dinner on the run.</i><br> <br>Disgusting. A pigsty? I’d strongly advise you to clean up your nasty mess, Em! Babies should not be exposed to that filth.<br> <br><b>Constant ’widening eyes’ and ‘giggling’</b><br>I have noticed numerous times by now that fictional characters widen their eyes all the time and they have the tendency to giggle too much as well. I tried it out myself but I never widen my eyes. I’m clueless why anyone would do that because it’s very odd. And excessively giggling women don’t do anything for me either.<br> <br><b>Huge interrogation mark</b><br>Honestly, it’s a mystery to me why Aidan and Em’s story would need a sequel. Oh, wait, the only reason is…<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>$__$</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Naturally it goes without saying that I won’t be reading the next installment.<br> <br><b>Overall verdict</b><br>Emma, get your act together and if you are in need of some company then just buy a dog and spare me your histrionics. Thank you.<br> <br> <br><b>As a side note</b><br>Everyone loved this book. Maybe this is another case of “It’s not the book it’s me.”<br> <br> <br> <br><i>
  <b>**Review at request of author, Katie Ashley**</b>
</i><br><br> <br> <br> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

You broke my heart.. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/457822.gif" width="482" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The worst of all....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/663445.gif" width="495" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, you thickheaded......... male! I adore you!! And Emma worshiped the ground you walked upon...<br><br><b>You'd better spent the next book grovelling!!!!!!!!!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393983i/758585.jpg" width="500" height="334" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*RUNNING OFF TO READ THE NEXT AND THANK GOD I WAITED FOR IT TO COME OUT TO READ THE SERIES*</b><br><br>Almost forgot! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6546441.Katie_Ashley" title="Katie Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Katie Ashley</a><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380369805ra/722544.gif" width="500" height="214" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_445406717" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445406717" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3820197-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383385041p2/3820197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445406717?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/3820197-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820197-jill?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820197-jill?shelf=2012-debuts">2012-debuts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445406717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14226235043483613444"><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Emma Harrison is pushing thirty and desperate to have a baby. With no partner, she has made an arrangement with her gay best friend, Connor to be her sperm donor. But Connor's partner is not in favour of the idea, and Connor reneges. <br/><br/>Aidan Fitzgerald, renowned for his <i>screw-em-and-leave-em</i> policy where women are concerned, works in marketing at the same firm as Emma. When Aidan finds out that she is wanting to conceive, he graciously offers his services as stud. <br/><br/>So, what did I like abou</span>
  <span id="freeText14226235043483613444" style="display:none"><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Emma Harrison is pushing thirty and desperate to have a baby. With no partner, she has made an arrangement with her gay best friend, Connor to be her sperm donor. But Connor's partner is not in favour of the idea, and Connor reneges. <br /><br />Aidan Fitzgerald, renowned for his <i>screw-em-and-leave-em</i> policy where women are concerned, works in marketing at the same firm as Emma. When Aidan finds out that she is wanting to conceive, he graciously offers his services as stud. <br /><br />So, what did I like about <i>The Proposition</i>? The heroine. Emma was really likable. She's definitely one of the better contemporary romance heroines. She's successful, and pretty much an altogether person. And how about this? She believes sex should be part of love, commitment, a relationship. Don't read that too often!<br /><br />The hero. Aidan is cocky, a bit of a jerk, a little full of himself but in a cute way. He's sweet, funny, considerate and he loves kids. Just not his own! Aidan thankfully is not an overbearing alpha control freak that seems to be dominating romance hero-dom at present. My only real complaint about him is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Please Fitzy, can you call lovemaking something other than a f*ck! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />Going into this I knew that the heroine was wanting a baby as a single parent. Having children is of course one of the greatest responsibilities ever, and yields some of the greatest rewards. Single parenthood I should imagine is not something to consider lightly. I completely understand her desire for a baby, yet Emma had given up hope of finding a man with whom she could have a baby and family, and she wasn't even thirty? <br /><br />And although Aidan and Emma knew each other, they had never been out on a date. But their first evening together Aidan offers up his sperm. No I'll-consider-this-deeply. Or, perhaps I should get some advice from a counsellor. Maybe read up on the responsibilities and expectations of being a sperm donor.<br /><br />Connor spills the beans to Aidan about Emma wanting a baby after knowing him all of five minutes! Blabber mouth! Then Aidan when extolling his virtues as a donor says, <i>"My family doesn't have a history of any major diseases."</i> Really?? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Um, your mother died of cancer, Aidan! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The prose is average to good. The beginning scenes between Emma and Aidan could have been fleshed out more, given more details. Their arrangement seemed to happen all too quickly. <br /><br />But overall the story was fun, sexy, steamy. The developing romance was really well done, as we see them falling in love gradually over time. Their relationship grew believably and sweetly. And we're also given some much appreciated scenes from Aidan's point-of-view. <br /><br /><b>Warning! Will Robinson!</b><br />This story does not end with a HEA. There is a cliffhanger and the sequel <i>The Proposal</i>, will be out in January. I know a lot of romance readers are tiring of cliffhangers and sequels. But it actually didn't bother me. <br /><br />The other issue that may affect some readers is the 'cheating' incident. I personally didn't even see this particular scene as cheating. But, we all have different levels of tolerance.<br /><br />I did toss up between 3.5 and 4 stars. But I think most readers of CR will love this (4 or even 5 stars). <i>The Proposition</i> was entertaining, a sweet romance and a little different to the usual CRs that are around at the moment. And I enjoyed it enough that I want to read the sequel. <br /><br /><b>Steam:</b> 3-3.5<br /><br /><i>ARC courtesy of Katie Ashley</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14226235043483613444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_451253896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451253896" />
    <a title="Rachel (BAVR)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6303796-rachel-bavr"><img alt="Rachel (BAVR)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396635700p2/6303796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/451253896?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (BAVR)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (BAVR)" href="/user/show/6303796-rachel-bavr">Rachel (BAVR)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16126502-the-proposition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=angst-city">angst-city</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=blame-bavr">blame-bavr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=dead-spouse-baggage">dead-spouse-baggage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=fluffy-cottonballs">fluffy-cottonballs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=longshanks-mcgiantwang">longshanks-mcgiantwang</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=self-esteem-crisis">self-esteem-crisis</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=things-that-don-t-make-sense">things-that-don-t-make-sense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=too-wtf-to-resist">too-wtf-to-resist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer451253896&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451253896" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4318484753646581260"><b>WARNING: Major spoilers ahead! I'm not kidding. I'm going to spoil the ending. Also: GIFs because some emotions are beyond words.</b><br/><br/>Basically, <i>The Proposition</i> is a baby fantasy Harley with more pages and 80% more orgasms. If that kind of book skeeves you out the way it does me, then this book probably isn't for you.<br/><br/>The heroine in <i>The Proposition</i> doesn't understand female biology in the slightest. If that kind of trope pisses you off, then this book probably isn't for you.<br/><br/>The ending of <i>The Propositi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4318484753646581260" style="display:none"><b>WARNING: Major spoilers ahead! I'm not kidding. I'm going to spoil the ending. Also: GIFs because some emotions are beyond words.</b><br><br>Basically, <i>The Proposition</i> is a baby fantasy Harley with more pages and 80% more orgasms. If that kind of book skeeves you out the way it does me, then this book probably isn't for you.<br><br>The heroine in <i>The Proposition</i> doesn't understand female biology in the slightest. If that kind of trope pisses you off, then this book probably isn't for you.<br><br>The ending of <i>The Proposition</i> is a FUCKING CLIFFHANGER, leaving the reader at the mercy of one or god forbid TWO sequels to get to a Happily Ever After. If that kind of shameless money-grubbing bullshit makes you want to pull your hair out, then this book probably isn't for you.<br><br><b>A Visual Illustration of How This Book Made Me Feel</b><br><a href="http://s1051.beta.photobucket.com/user/rachelc138/library/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396933ra/765505.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>An Intentionally Brief Summary of <i>The Proposition</i></b><br>Emotionally unstable Mary Sue decides to heal all of her personal problems with a baby. Emotionally immature playboy agrees to make a baby with her because he wants to get in her panties. SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX SEX! Nothing happens. They conceive. Nothing happens but SEX SEX SEX SEX, etc. Emotionally unstable Mary Sue does the emotionally unstable Mary Sue thing and falls in love. Emotionally immature playboy fears all the feelings he's feeling. Spectacular douche move in the last pages of the book that would have made for a very satisfying ending if you're like me and didn't care about the characters. Then BAM! Cliffhanger. Buy the next book, bitches! <br><br>There is nothing about Emma and Aidan's story that warrants a sequel. This isn't Lord of the Rings. It's just a story about two hot people fucking a lot that could potentially fill women over the age of 30 with the heroine's bullshit neurosis. I think the story should end as it did in this book. It struck me as both the most realistic part of the story and fucking hilarious. Seriously, I just laughed and laughed the whole way through the heart-breaking scene in which Aidan destroys everything just by being the guy he says he's been along. Who needs weapons in modern warfare when poor puppies like Aidan can destroy entire lives simply through the weight of their emotional baggage? <br><br>Guys Like Aidan:<br><a href="http://s1051.beta.photobucket.com/user/rachelc138/library/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396933ra/765506.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In a big shift from my usual feelings about heroes in contemporary romance, I didn't mind Aidan all that much. Sure, the wealthy, drop-dead gorgeous, sex god character is totally overdone these days, but Aidan has the advantage of not being a possessive asshole. He's really quite sweet when he isn't whinging inexplicably about commitment and destroying everything. Despite coming from a good family and leading a pretty standard life devoid of most forms of asshattery, Aidan fears emotional commitments like marriage and children above all else. I'm still not sure why. I can see a man in his thirties not <i>wanting</i> to settle down and have children because he just isn't into that stuff, but Aidan contradicts that by launching his peen into Emma's baby-crazy vagina and deciding that he wants "more" with her. All the while, he cowers in terror at the thought of love, marriage, and the baby that he totally makes with Emma and can't take back even with all the wishes in the world. <br><br>Basically, Aidan's an irrational dick. And in the end, he does exactly what an irrational dick would do. After realizing that he's in love with Emma, Aidan totally freaks out, withdraws, and attempts to have sex with the first woman who expresses interest in his love stick. He takes the woman back to his house, a place where Emma frequents because she's the clingy girlfriend of his worst nightmares, and they try to have sex. Note my use of the word <i>try</i>. Naturally, because the poor lady isn't his TWU LUV Emma, he can't even get it up. And just when he's about to cut out the foreplay because he totally isn't feeling it ... <b>Emma arrives!</b> It's the most pathetic scene ever. The poor woman even picked up his dog from doggy daycare because she's the type of lady who will take care of Aidan forever and probably knit him socks in the winter, but he just can't deal. <br><br>While I should have been pissed at Aidan for his behavior, I had to appreciate Katie Ashley's willingness to <i>go there</i>. Aidan ends up doing exactly what he's said he would do all along, even despite their TWU LUV. Sometimes, great sex and mushy feelings aren't enough to keep a man-boy from acting like a man-boy. I was thrilled with this bittersweet ending for all of, like, 30 seconds before I realized that the sickly sweet story I'd been reading up until that point wasn't going to end without a Happily Ever After. <br><br>Then I got cliffhangered. <br><br>And why? Because Emma sucks. <br><br>From the beginning, Emma grated on my nerves. Self-absorbed, overly emotional, and insecure, this woman is horrible from the opening scene when she throws a baby shower for a co-worker and uses that as an opportunity to cry about being 29 and childless to the ending when she decides to fight for her man because a shit-tastic wreck like Aidan is SO WORTH HAVING. Following in the Mary Sue tradition of being an orphan, Emma spends a lot of time whining about her dead parents, her dead fiance, and all the babies she isn't having. She feels the biological clock ticking down to her 30th birthday, and she just can't take it anymore. <br><br>You have to understand, my friends, that aside from being 18 kind of wacka-doodle-doo, Emma also seems to possess the same understanding of female biology as that Congressman who claimed that women can shut down their reproductive systems in the case of "legitimate" rape. Unless they're 30, in which case shutting down a reproductive system isn't even necessary because Emma thinks they CAN'T HAVE BABIES. Sure, she doesn't outright say that, but from the way she switches from emotional breakdown to emotional breakdown because she's just so goddamn OLD and BARREN, I'm pretty sure that's what she really thinks. How insulting. I know plenty of women who have conceived after the age of 30, even into their 40s. This isn't the first time I've seen this trope in contemporary romance, and it needs to stop already. Women do not become worthless, dried-out husks after their 20s. They just don't. Stop writing that, authors. Stop it. <br><br>Emma decides she MUST HAVE BABY NOW for probably the worst reason anyone could have a baby. Like, this rates right up there with people who conceive to save their marriages. Emma wants a baby because she wants to replace all the dead people in her life. She wants to basically force a person into existence who has no choice but to love her and fill her emotional voids. Getting professional help for her grief issues before making a baby isn't a priority to Emma, nor is actually finding a person to create a family with. Oh, no. <b>Emma want baby. Emma want baby NOW.</b> At first, she sets her baby-making sights on her gay best friend. She basically puts a claim out on his sperm and then has a total meltdown when <i>his</i> boyfriend doesn't want to share all of those valuable swimmer in her unhealthy little scheme. <br><br>Fortunately for Emma, Aidan steps in to do the job. Unfortunately for Emma, her emotional cray-cray level pretty much guarantees that she'll become attached to Aidan through hundreds of flowery orgasms and get her heart broken. All of this comes to pass. <br><br>So, Emma goes all-in emotionally with Aidan. He cheats on her while she's <b>pregnant with his child</b>. Then, proving that she's learned NOTHING about self-respect and emotional stability for the sake of her child, she agrees to team up with Aidan's sister (?) to win her man. And this is done by adding another book to the series. <br><br>My dreams have imploded, and all that's left is dust, dust, dust ...<br><br>On the bright side, this book isn't as poorly written as On Dublin Street. Granted, there are still plenty of typos, missing words, and misused punctuation. Katie Ashley seems to have a grasp on the written word, though, so I'll give her credit. Without the entertainment of Aidan's spectacular douche move at the end, this probably would have been one star. Sadly, I doubt I'll be buying the next book in the series. I have no desire to read another verbose description of why Emma and Aidan really shouldn't procreate. That poor baby. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4318484753646581260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer787262706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8514457214777934177"><b>Rating : 3.5 ‘Lovely’ Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422188763i/13469139._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>My Views :</b> Throughout the book the one word that was playing in my mind was <b>LOVELY</b>. This book was lovely, no big Drama, good amount of laughter, sarcasm, a little tension here and there, nice friendship, a<b> dirty mouth hero </b> and a sweet heroine…Overall it was a good read but nothing new that blew me.<br/><br/><b>Style of writing :</b> I loved her style of writing as she managed to keep me rooted on my seat and my eyes didn’t bulge from my kindle…so YES Katie you totally rocked. This is </span>
  <span id="freeText8514457214777934177" style="display:none"><b>Rating : 3.5 ‘Lovely’ Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422188763i/13469139._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My Views :</b> Throughout the book the one word that was playing in my mind was <b>LOVELY</b>. This book was lovely, no big Drama, good amount of laughter, sarcasm, a little tension here and there, nice friendship, a<b> dirty mouth hero </b> and a sweet heroine…Overall it was a good read but nothing new that blew me.<br><br><b>Style of writing :</b> I loved her style of writing as she managed to keep me rooted on my seat and my eyes didn’t bulge from my kindle…so YES Katie you totally rocked. This is my first book from this author and I must say that she did impress me…and the sex was *fanning myself* Hot.<br><br><b>Characters :</b> Aidan was *Lick Lips*…yes let me hide my inner slut but Aidan was that good. He wasn’t different from other manwhores out there but his sweetness towards Emma totally made me swoon. Yes that last bit was a bit ‘Douchbaggy’ (I’ll take the liberty with this word) but overall he was cocky and I love Cocky.<br><br><b>“A MWF sex schedule? How efficient," he mused.<br>"Please be serious."<br>A wicked grin flashed on his face. "Fine, pencil me in. I'll be ready and erect whenever you need me.”</b><br><br>On the other hand Emma was the sweet heroine who brought out the best in Aidan and finally cracked the walls of his heart and made him fall in love…Haven’t we heard that before. Yes I know <b>Cliché </b><br><br><b>Favorite Part :</b> I loved the part where they go to meet Emma’s BIG Family…If I could dive into those pages and be with that family, believe me I would have done that…Because at each line I was like “Aww that’s so sweet” and I couldn’t swipe that stupid smile off my face (which totally earned the book 0.5 Stars...What!!! I’m being Honest)<br><br><b>What did not work?</b> I found that the book was nothing different from I’ve read previously…The storyline where manwhore meets good girl, then behaves properly towards the girl because he can’t stand to hurt her feelings...It starts as friendship but both fell in love with the other secretly…Finally one or the other fuck up (normally the guy!!), then the pacifying and winning of heart blah blah…Too much Cliché<br><br>I honestly think that cliffy was not needed...she could have ended that book in 10 more pages. <br><br>Am I going to read the next book..well maybe when I will not have anything interesting to read then ;)<br><br><b> Similar books? </b> The sperm donor / pregnant storyline no!!!<br>But the rest…every second book.<br><br><b> Recommended :</b> Yes, it was a nice read…I need something light and this one did lighten my mood.<br><br><a href="http://peekatmybookreview.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="description" height="60" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418569189i/12827092._SX540_.jpg" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img alt="description" height="60" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418816316i/12909941.png" width="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_430309229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430309229" />
    <a title="Kim Person" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7590856-kim-person"><img alt="Kim Person" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434694589p2/7590856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430309229?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim Person" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim Person" href="/user/show/7590856-kim-person">Kim Person</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430309229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5090594305046329769">When I found out that Katie was going to provide me the ARC of The Proposition I was like......<br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393714ra/758068.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>This is the story of Emma & Aidan. Emma's a kind hearted, sweet, and strong as hell woman and I loved her character! She has been through some very rough times in the past 5 years and all she wants is a baby! She is desperate to have a baby and have a "family" of her own .....someone to love her! Well after her best friend since middle school Connor backs out of "donating" to the cause Emma is not happ</span>
  <span id="freeText5090594305046329769" style="display:none">When I found out that Katie was going to provide me the ARC of The Proposition I was like......<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393714ra/758068.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>This is the story of Emma &amp; Aidan. Emma's a kind hearted, sweet, and strong as hell woman and I loved her character! She has been through some very rough times in the past 5 years and all she wants is a baby! She is desperate to have a baby and have a "family" of her own .....someone to love her! Well after her best friend since middle school Connor backs out of "donating" to the cause Emma is not happy and Connor, well, he hates that Emma is ignoring him. <br><br>Aidan Fitzgerald just happens to be in the right place at the right time and witnesses the exchange between Emma and Connor but mistakes it for something else. But Connnor will set him straight and Aidan being the hot, sexy as hell, player (according to office place gossip) now has the solution to get what he wants. Aidan wants Emma and has since the office Christmas party where she shot him down after she was told he was a "womanizer". <br><br>Over drinks at O'Malley's the proposition is made and Emma is stunned but she's right about Aidan he is going to get something out of this and that is Emma.. He's not "donating" he is "participating" So begins the baby making journey..<br><br>How could Emma resist Aidan?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379792957i/570861.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are some very hot scenes between the sheets, shower well I'm sure you get the picture and once Emma gets pregnant well the ride is too much fun for either of the to get off, just yet, see they never expected or at least tried to keep their hearts out of it but come on we all know how that goes...<br><br>Aidan well for all he supposedly is really has a heart of gold but boy there was a point in the book where I was like this because of him<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393714ra/758069.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are some wonderful secondary characters in the book and I adored Carli &amp; Connor who were there for Emma. Aidan has his four sisters and "Pop's". We get to enjoy Emma &amp; Aidan meeting each others families and there are some great laughs but there is something about Aidan who has had his share of heartbreak in the past, self created I might add, that made me:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393714ra/758070.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aidan is afraid of committment becoming the ultimate bachelor but will he let Emma &amp; his baby become a permanent part of his life? or will he be Aidan well that my friends you will hae just read to see!!<br><br>Katie has given us a 5 star awesome read!! I cannot wait for the second book and I will anxiously await the announcement for when that is coming hint hint Katie :) This is a AWESOME first book and I can guarantee you wil be hooked just as I am! So come November 1st buy this book and start the journey with Emma &amp; Aidan you won't be disappointed I sure the heck wasn't I've read the book twice already since last night :)<br><br>Thanks for sharing Katie love ya doll!!!<br><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16062211.The_Proposition" title="The Proposition by Katie Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer729298475&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer729298475" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer374016173526872529">WARNING/SWEARING/SPOILERS <br/><br/>I read this book a while ago, but haven't posted my rating yet..<br/><br/>so hear we go...... <br/><br/>I decided to read this book on the basis that my curiosity got the better of me, as the pregnancy theme was interesting and i wanted to see what resolution would the author come up with, but sadly there was no resolution and it got worst by the cheating.<br/><br/>1. Let me start with the book...Why the author have to use the plot device based on heavy amount of casual slut shaming and sexualised t</span>
  <span id="freeText374016173526872529" style="display:none">WARNING/SWEARING/SPOILERS <br /><br />I read this book a while ago, but haven't posted my rating yet..<br /><br />so hear we go...... <br /><br />I decided to read this book on the basis that my curiosity got the better of me, as the pregnancy theme was interesting and i wanted to see what resolution would the author come up with, but sadly there was no resolution and it got worst by the cheating.<br /><br />1. Let me start with the book...Why the author have to use the plot device based on heavy amount of casual slut shaming and sexualised the hero? Why are the qualities confining a man such as: leadership, honesty, commitment and respect are suddenly not good enough any more??? Obviously the author's imagination ran short. But it is not just the hero I am disappointed with but also the heroin's immaturity was completely out of place considering her adulthood age...<br /><br />2. I got the idea of Aidan to be portrait it as a manslut, non-committal type of guy, but what I don't understand is why then put him in a situation when it is clear he is not the right guy to live up to the expectations??? Although I disliked his slut-shaming, Emma knew exactly what to expect of him or shall i say what not to expect of him, so she can partially blamed herself for this course of events. Back to Aidan, I think what he did was wrong, by not confronting his true feelings and his reaction to take Eamma out of his system was just lame, poor excuse in my book! If a guy tells you.. <br /><br />“You know you’re the only one I want, right?” and then admitting to himself.... <br /><br />"In the end, maybe it didn’t matter if he loved her. He could not imagine giving up the entirety of his life to being all she would need. To be choked by the responsibility of being a husband and father…fuck no." <br /><br />LET ME TELL YOU...It means he is deceiving this person and is not capable of developing a healthy, stable and emotional relationship, so WHY on earht he is telling that person that she is the only person he wants??? His resolution for not embracing his feelings for Emma was dishonest, poor and distasteful...why does the guy has to cheat in order to get the woman he loves out of his mind? can he just be honest with her or just walk away from her? Why does his playboy reputation grant him excuse for cheating? OK he is known for his man-whoring ways so the reader must assume it is to be expected of him???? NO NO IT IS NOT OK to act like that....regardless of your past. By fully intending to have sex with that woman, Aiden was selfish by thinking that he could forget about his commitment to Emma not even considering her feelings and instead confront his predicament in responsible way he just cheapened their love by lowering it to one sexual encounter with a woman that would be enough to brush it of...So love to him can be easily forgotten by one sex with a woman...HOW NARROW MINDED HE IS!<br /><br />3. Emma: I just could not understand her motives....WHY ON EARTH she would want to have a child with a man that would not commit to relationship and is not ready to become a father figure??? How can she expose her child for that lack of fatherhood and why does she had to do this at the age of 30??? Although i condemn what Aidan did, Emma should not be surprise considering his reputation and past.<br /><br />My final thought is that cheating should not be that easy forgiven...although we are humans it is not excuse to just brush it of like it did not happened and I could assume that will happen with the second installment....In my book, how do you respect yourself staying with a man who can't or won't value you? I wish Emma decided to leave him because she's not the one giving up on the relationship, Aiden gave up on it when he cheated, deciding to take her out of his system. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3141495620480365626"><br/>★★★★ <b>4 stars!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397154040i/9238791.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book has been on my TBR for over a year and I'm so glad I finally decided to give it a try! It was fun, engaging, steamy, original and at times, hilarious. Once I started it, I could not put it down until I knew how it would end and well, after that ending I immediately had to start <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16117804.The_Proposal__The_Proposition___2_' title='The Proposal (The Proposition, #2) by Katie Ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Proposal</a>. The fact that the MC's where in their thirties and trying to conceive gave them a more mature feel and the content was a nice change from the usual twenty something/college main charac</span>
  <span id="freeText3141495620480365626" style="display:none"><br>★★★★ <b>4 stars!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397154040i/9238791.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book has been on my TBR for over a year and I'm so glad I finally decided to give it a try! It was fun, engaging, steamy, original and at times, hilarious. Once I started it, I could not put it down until I knew how it would end and well, after that ending I immediately had to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16117804.The_Proposal__The_Proposition___2_" title="The Proposal (The Proposition, #2) by Katie Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Proposal</a>. The fact that the MC's where in their thirties and trying to conceive gave them a more mature feel and the content was a nice change from the usual twenty something/college main characters. <br><br><br><b>Emma -</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387510653ra/7610147.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Emma Harrison</b> is a 30 year old single woman who's biological clock has been ticking for years. She's an easy to like, independent heroine with a great sense of humor and I was really rooting for her to get her happy ending. Ever since her late fiancé died in a car accident four years ago, she's been single and patiently waiting for the right husband/father material to come along but so far, she's had no such luck. Her desire to become a mother is so great, she's even willing to ask her gay best friend to donate his sperm. But then comes the perfect solution in the form of Aidan Fitzgerald. <br><br><b>Aidan -</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397154040ra/9238792.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Aidan Fitzgerald</b> is a 32 year old handsome bachelor who's had a thing for Emma ever since seeing her at the company's Christmas party a few months ago. His player-reputation prevented him from ever having a chance at seducing her, but now that he knows she's looking for someone to father her baby and nothing more, he comes up with a <u>proposition</u>: He will father Emma's child, but she must conceive it with him naturally. <br><br>After a while their baby-making sessions become more than just physical and they both start to reevaluate the nature of their arrangement. At first, I wasn't sure I liked Aidan, but throughout the story, he really grew on me. He won me over with his sweet and considerate behavior and after a while it seemed as if he might be willing to change his playboy ways for Emma and his future child.<br><br>So, as the story went on, it remained fairly drama-less and with very little angst, but then the last 10% of the story, my feelings went from:<br><br><b>Slightly agitated and highly suspicious...</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397154040ra/9238793.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>To upset and slightly shocked...</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397154040ra/9238794.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>To even more upset and angry.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397154040ra/9238795.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But despite his asshole behavior, I have a feeling Aidan will make me like him again in no time. Although, he'll have some serieus groveling to do first...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397162400ra/9240441.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Moving on to the next book right away!</b></span>

<div id="review_444369198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/444369198" />
    <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie"><img alt="Natasha is a Book Junkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585046882p2/9389992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444369198?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha is a Book Junkie" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie">Natasha is a Book Junkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16126502-the-proposition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444369198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9063617599140662244"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Here’s my proposition. I offer to father your child, and you in turn, promise to conceive it with me naturally.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Just when I thought another romance novel couldn’t possibly surprise me - <b>Ladies and Gentlemen, lo and behold, The Proposition!!</b> A perfect ratio of sweet and romantic, a super-sized amount of scorching <i>hot lovin’</i> and convincing sexual chemistry, with just a dash of angst, this is the perfect recipe for the type of story that will please anyone looking for a book to curl up</span>
  <span id="freeText9063617599140662244" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Here’s my proposition. I offer to father your child, and you in turn, promise to conceive it with me naturally.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Just when I thought another romance novel couldn’t possibly surprise me - <b>Ladies and Gentlemen, lo and behold, The Proposition!!</b> A perfect ratio of sweet and romantic, a super-sized amount of scorching <i>hot lovin’</i> and convincing sexual chemistry, with just a dash of angst, this is the perfect recipe for the type of story that will please anyone looking for a book to curl up with and escape into, all the while having a goofy grin plastered all over your satisfied face. Piece of advice though - do NOT forget to have an industrial-sized fan handy because <i>it’s</i> <i>gonna get hot</i>!!<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Have you ever wanted something so bad you think you’d die if you didn’t have it? That the mere thought of it keeps you up at night. You can’t sleep, you can’t eat, you can’t drink. You are so consumed by that desire nothing else matters, and you’re not sure life is worth living if you can’t have it.”</i>
</blockquote>Emma is a thirty-year-old single woman who wishes nothing more than to have a baby of her own. Her dreams of becoming a mother have almost become a physical need for her, making her willing to do almost anything to make that happen, desperate enough to even ask her gay best friend to father her child. But when everything falls through with that arrangement, the answer to all her prayers comes in the form of Aidan, a man whose womanizing reputation precedes him by a mile.<br /><br />Aidan is a player. Aidan doesn’t do relationships. Aidan equates the responsibility of being a husband and father to choking. Emma is also the only woman who has ever rejected his advances and he is willing to do just about anything to get her into his bed. But that is not the only reason Aidan offers his ‘stud services’ to Emma - he is no stranger to the kind of comforting feeling that the love of a family can give you so he understands Emma’s need to become a mother. His motives might be primarily fueled by his raging libido, but there is a part of him that connects with Emma and desires nothing more than to make her happy.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You’ve had so much death and loss that you just want a little life in you.”</i>
</blockquote><br />At this point I recommend bringing that industrial-sized fan out of storage and turning it on at full blast because Ms Ashley writes good sex scenes like nobody’s business. Emma and Aidan engage in a commitment-free physical relationship aimed at one thing and one thing only - making a baby for Emma. Let me tell you, as a reader, it has never been so much fun reaping the benefits of a fictional arrangement like this before! The chemistry between our lead characters is unquestionable, the connection created by their toe-curling sexual encounters slowly bleeding into other areas of their lives, making them fall for each other for all the right reasons and fighting to stay emotionally unattached for all the wrong ones. They don’t reach that point at the same time, or rather they don’t realize the depth of their feelings for each other simultaneously, but once their emotional bond is forged, all they can do is deny it to themselves and to each other.<br /><br />This is in so many ways Emma’s story, and a very personal one at that. Unless you’ve ever been ‘an Emma' in your life, it might be difficult to imagine what it is like to face the unwanted prospect of never holding your own baby in your arms. So many of Emma’s emotions in this book felt very familiar, identifiable, real. Her hopeless desire to become a mother took central stage even in her relationship with Aidan, making her willing to suppress her growing feelings for him in order to fulfill her dream of having a baby. She threads so very carefully with him, always aware of his commitment phobias and trying not to push him into anything he is not ready for.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Their entire relationship was such a fragile balloon that she was afraid would pop at any moment.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Aidan is a much more complicated character than Emma. This might be Emma’s story but it is Aidan’s journey to travel. His ‘conversion’ from incorrigible bachelor to man owning up to his feelings is a slowly progressing one, laced with doubt, inner conflict and a desperate want to avoid commitment at all costs. I hope we get to delve into the reasons behind this urge to form no lasting ties with a woman in the sequel as I found that part of his personality as fascinating as it was infuriating.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Love like he had never known entered him that day, and instead of embracing it, he kept railing against it. … In the end, maybe it didn’t matter if he loved her. He could not imagine giving up the entirety of his life to being all she would need.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Ms Ashley’s writing style is a force to be reckoned with. Apart from the spectacular dialogues which, in my opinion, can make or break a story, this book is flawlessly written in its entirety, leaving me with no objections other than having to wait to have the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16117804-the-proposal" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Proposal</a>, in my greedy little hands. This is a story you will love from the very first page and will want to re-read right after you finished it. It will leave the romance junkie in you well sated but also craving for more. More of everything.<br /><br />~ N ♥<br /><br /><a href="http://wp.me/p2AtqW-BB" rel="nofollow noopener">See this review on my blog!</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/natashaisabookjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Facebook!</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9063617599140662244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
