<div id="review_448390350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/448390350" />
    <a title="~ Becs ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2626261-becs"><img alt="~ Becs ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388693144p2/2626261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/448390350?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~ Becs ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~ Becs ~" href="/user/show/2626261-becs">~ Becs ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=shower-smexin">shower-smexin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=shy-heroine">shy-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer448390350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13466507663822316071">This is quite simply a fantastic debut novel by Katie Ashley. If love, laughter and passion are the hallmarks of a truly great romance, then The Proposition ticks every box. With a central duo to really believe in and cherish and also to despair with, a great host of secondary characters that are well crafted and feel real and an intriguing premise for a plot, this is quite the accomplished debut and Katie Ashley has proved herself a consummate storyteller. It’s very engaging and captivating; it</span>
  <span id="freeText13466507663822316071" style="display:none">This is quite simply a fantastic debut novel by Katie Ashley. If love, laughter and passion are the hallmarks of a truly great romance, then The Proposition ticks every box. With a central duo to really believe in and cherish and also to despair with, a great host of secondary characters that are well crafted and feel real and an intriguing premise for a plot, this is quite the accomplished debut and Katie Ashley has proved herself a consummate storyteller. It’s very engaging and captivating; it caught my attention right from the first page and, with the witty dialogue, I was engrossed right through to the very end.<br><br>Basic Synopsis – Emma’s 30th birthday is looming large on the horizon and her biological clock is ticking so loud it’s deafening her and everyone around her. After her gay best friend refuses to be a sperm donor, Aidan Fitzgerald, known manwhore and womanizer, offers to jump into the breach with just one condition – the baby must be conceived naturally. He’s been attracted to Emma for a long time and, blinded by his easy charm and desperate to conceive, she agrees.<br><br>Aidan was a great hero – he’s cocky, charming and more than a little misunderstood but he is commitment-shy and has a bit of a reputation with the ladies. I was leery of how their first night of babymaking would go but I needn’t have worried. Aidan, sensible of the strangeness of their situation, made it very romantic and the writing builds the anticipation well until the pyrotechnics go off. Seriously HOT! There’s some great humour in here too as they work out their sex schedule.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“A MWF sex schedule? How efficient,” he mused. <br>“Please be serious.”<br>A wicked grin flashed on his face. “Fine, pencil me in. I’ll be ready and erect whenever you need me.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Emma is a sweetheart of a heroine – completely honest, without guile and a little bit heartbroken by losses in her past, I very much identified with her. She never really ever seemed desperate, just sad and lonely. She has great friends too and both she and Aidan have loving families which we get to know and – a quick word about the secondary characters. So often in novels, these aren’t fully developed and feel like cardboard cutouts but that’s quite simply not the case here – they jumped instantly to life off the pages and it all felt very real.<br><br>But, the course of true love never did run smooth and there are some bumps in the road ahead as Emma finds herself falling for Aidan who is in complete denial of his emotions and scared to death of commitment.<br><br>It’s a fantastic debut novel but I will warn you all – MAJOR WICKED CLIFFHANGER ALERT!<br><br><a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380396494i/764312.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is happening with increasing frequency in romance novels lately and I guess it’s a ploy to leave you salivating for more. Well, IT WORKED! Now I can’t wait for the sequel – The Proposal.<br><br>4.5 stars contemporary romance<br><br><i>ARC courtesy of the lovely Katie Ashley</i><br><br><i>For more reviews, please visit <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Reviews</a></i></span>

  <span id="freeText17846468224213034694" style="display:none">Spoiler Free Review<br />4 STARS out of 5<br />Genre: Contemporary Romance<br /><br /><b>Love love loved this book!!!<br /><br />TICK<br />TOCK<br />TICK<br />TOCK <br />That's the sound of Emma's biological clock.</b><br /><br />Emma Harrison is approaching her 30th birthday and wants nothing more in this world than to have a family. Unfortunately she is not currently dating anyone. Finding a good man to marry and procreate with may take years. But it only takes 9 months to have a baby via the sperm bank. Emma realizes that she may not have the man of her dreams yet; but she could still find love with a child of her own.<br />Loss has plagued her life for the past five years and all Emma wants is to fill the emptiness left behind by the ones she loved. When plans start to fall through Emma is upset and gets in to an argument with her close friend, Conner. This leads to her crying hysterically and bringing the last person she would ever expect to her rescue.... Aiden Fitzgerald.<br /><br /><b>Not him, not NOW!</b><br /> Aiden is known as the company playboy and he makes sure to live up to that name. He exudes sex appeal, he displays his arrogance, is above and beyond egotistical, and can be a little impetuous. When Aiden takes an upset Emma out for a drink to help ease her nerves she gives him more than he bargained for... He get's her raw emotions in heart felt words.<br /><br /><i>“Have you ever wanted something so bad you think you’d die if you don’t have it? That the mere thought of it keeps you up at night. You can’t sleep, you can’t eat, you can’t drink. You are so consumed by that desire nothing else matters, and you’re not sure life is worth living if you can’t have it.”</i> ~Emma<br /><br />This causes him to open up as well. Then he comes up with a plan that will fulfill both of their needs.<br /><br /><b>Oh baby I like it<i> RAW!</i></b> <br /> Aiden ends the night with a proposition... Clearly thinking with his little head and not the big one; Aiden agrees to be Emma's sperm donor. All Emma has to do is conceive the child naturally. Meaning he wants<b> raw, hot, passionate SEX!</b> **Grinning**<br /><br />What starts off as a clear business deal with a signed contract ends in a SHOCKINGLY HEARTBREAKING CLIFFHANGER.<br /> Yes, I said CLIFFHANGER and YES, I F**KING HATE that word too.<br /><br />I am definitely feeling your style Katie Ashley. You gave me a nice dose of just about everything I need in a Contemporary romance. I got the hilarious, fun, loving and vivacious best friend, in Casey. The Gay best friend, in Conner. A pet dog that takes the spotlight whenever he is around, in Beau. Heartwarming family moments. And a breath taking, heart stopping man who falls for a gorgeous woman that is<b>
  <i> 'the total package.'</i>
</b>  Needless to say I LOVED IT!!!<br /><br /><u>Fave Lines</u><br /><br /><i>"A MWF sex schedule? How efficient,"</i> he mused<br /><i>"Please be serious."<br />"Fine, pencil me in. I'll be ready and erect whenever you need me."</i> <br />~Aiden and Emma<br /><br /><i>"Baby, you're so sexy when you spout that medical jargon."</i> ~Casey<br /><br /><u>Fave phrase</u><br /><br /><b>'Big Poppa'</b> - Term of endearment used by Casey and Connor when referring to Aiden<br /><br /><u>Best text EVAH sent</u><br /><br /><i>'Good. I'm looking forward to kissing and licking every square inch of that fabulous body tonight.'</i> ~Aiden<br /><br />Fave new word<br /><br /><b>'Gunkel'</b> - Meaning "gay uncle" <br /><br />My Ratings<br />Characters- Lovable<br />Writing Style- Witty, Sexy and Solid<br />Plot/Storyline- Fun and Savory<br />Steam Factor- High/Very Steamy<br />Overall- I loved it!! READ IT!!!<br /><b><br />Now go forth and read. Then come tell us about it on Goodreads!</b></span>

  <span id="freeText15874710791712633302" style="display:none">[This review will be gif-filled in honor of Katie, my fellow Gif whore. And yes, I’m talking about the author. And by the way, if you’re a kid, don’t read this.<br><br>Where shall I begin?<br><br>Emma Harrison wants a family and she wants it now. Tired of waiting for the right guy to start a family with she decides it’s time to take matters into her own hands. But getting a sperm donor might not be as easy as she thought it would be, especially when her best guy-friend refuses to cooperate. But what if… What if Connor is not her only option after all? What if there’s someone else willing to go along with her plans, as long as she agrees to a few conditions? How far will Emma go to have her dream of being a mom fulfilled? <br><br>Enter Aidan. Aidan Fitzgerald is cocky, arrogant, egotistical, self-centered, bigheaded, conceited, am I missing anything?… Okay,<i> okay!</i> I’m only kidding. I’m just a little mad at him, but we’ll get to that soon enough. Aidan is a little cocky yes, he’s way too hot for his own good, but you know how men are. Stoke his ego a little and you’ll only help to make it bigger… Let’s just say Aidan had a lot of stroking going on… and… stuff. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759339.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, I’m getting carried away. He’s good-looking and he knows it, so he uses it to his advantage to get whatever –and whoever –he wants. Aidan is not used to getting rejected, so when Emma wants nothing to do with him and his womanizing ways, well… it strucks a nerve, and makes him want her all that much. When the perfect opportunity to get what he wants is right in front of him, he will not hesitate to take it. No matter the cost. But did he stop to think about the consequences?<br><br>Against her better judgment Emma takes up Aidan’s proposition. But when emotions get in the way, is she really willing to risk her heart for a chance at motherhood? Is he even capable of changing his ways for her and his soon-to-be-born child? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just kidding. I’m not telling! You’ll have to read to find out.<br><br><i>The Proposition</i> made me feel all kinds of things. I understood Emma’s need to be a mother, her desire that run deeper than anything else, and I felt for her. Her pain and her love. And I got Aidan too, a little. After a difficult relationship in the past he closed off, he said no more to the pain and heartbreak, and I can go with that. What I can’t go with is him being an asshole because of it, and here lays the reason for my anger with him.<br><br>There was also a moment there that I really wanted to kick Aidan and make it impossible to be a father again. Yes, I was that angry at him. My heart was seriously beating out of my chest! All the time I kept thinking: <i>“he can’t do this to her, he can’t do this to her, damn it!”</i> but he was doing it and it was driving me crazy and I wanted to kill him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759341.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean… he could be so sweet and caring, even loving, one moment and then it was like he snapped out of it and was back to being his cold detached self. It irritated me a little. Mostly because he was threatening my happily ever after. Yes, <i>my</i> happily ever after.<br><br>Then there was Emma’s insecurities, too. I think some people will find this a little irritating, her need for constant reassurance, but I’ll give her credit. It’s not easy when you’re falling in love with someone that might just run away at the mere mention of commitment. <br><br>Overall <i>The Proposition</i> was seriously steamy, and sweet and nice and heartbreaking and shocking!<br><br>Yup, this is the moment I talk about the ending. So, get ready for some ranting (assuming you don’t consider all the rest ranting, that is).<br><br>I was really glad as I read on to find that there were no major twists that broke my heart completely, and as I neared the end I was beaming. <i>I’m going to have my happy ending!</i> I though, and well…<br><br>I should have known how it was going to end, really. Especially when I saw I only had two pages left and it was nowhere close to an ending, unless it was super rushed in… which it wasn’t. Let me tell you that I actually went around screaming and then <s>begged Katie to give me my last missing pages</s> asked Kaite if I was missing the ending of my copy. You can ask her. It’s the total truth. One word (okay, three): OH. MY. GOD!<br><br>That’s my ending reaction. Like…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759342.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383543ra/741755.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So yes, I think I need to be fair to the people that will read this when it’s released in like three days, so I’ll warn you now, there’s a cliffhanger. And I’ll warn you again, it will make you want to pull all your hair out and then maybe, just maybe stalk Katie until she tells you what will happen next. Not that I did. <s>Not that I won’t.</s><br><br>On a last note, and this goes to Katie: write fast, dude! I need the next book <i>now!</i> Or you’ll be responsible for my therapy sessions after this. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681938.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And no, don’t try that with authors that you don’t know or they can sue you. Maybe?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759344.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Katie, can I get a sneak peak? Something? Anything? Pretty please? Will do it for your gif-twin? Yes? <s>Maybe I should mention that my birthday is the 5th. *cough*</s><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394382ra/759345.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><s>Yes, I totally used that gif on purpose!</s><br><br>For more reviews, please visit <b>
  <a href="https://fictionaditction.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Through a Book</a>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3726530426226589384">This book is FANTASTIC! I absolutely love the premise, and let's be honest, I absolutely LOVE Aidan. Hello, hot stuff. He's sexy. He's confident. He knows his way around a woman's body. And it's an absolute delight to watch him fall (reluctantly) in love with our Emma.<br/><br/>There are so many wonderful, tender moments between these two characters. Aidan can be sweet. But I love how Ms. Ashley shows us that he's human and he can be an ass too. He's believable. <br/><br/>And have I mentioned that he's sexy? Yowza.</span>
  <span id="freeText3726530426226589384" style="display:none">This book is FANTASTIC! I absolutely love the premise, and let's be honest, I absolutely LOVE Aidan. Hello, hot stuff. He's sexy. He's confident. He knows his way around a woman's body. And it's an absolute delight to watch him fall (reluctantly) in love with our Emma.<br /><br />There are so many wonderful, tender moments between these two characters. Aidan can be sweet. But I love how Ms. Ashley shows us that he's human and he can be an ass too. He's believable. <br /><br />And have I mentioned that he's sexy? Yowza.<br /><br />The secondary characters are very well written as well. Emma's friends, including her gay best friend, are so funny. Emma and Aidan's families are both fun and loving and relatable. They are so well-integrated into the story that they don't feel like secondary characters at all, and that is not an easy thing to accomplish as a writer!<br /><br />I highly recommend this book. You'll smile, laugh, yell at your ereader (do NOT throw it across the room!) and fall in love with these people.<br /><br />Aidan is SEXY! :-)</span>

  <span id="freeText7991550712902589295" style="display:none">This book? This book was fan-freaking-tastic.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393127ra/756811.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I was lucky enough to read an ARC of The Proposition, and WOW-WOW-WEE-WOW! <div id="review_1498949108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498949108" />
    <a title="Henz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19767615-henz"><img alt="Henz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516450827p2/19767615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498949108?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henz" href="/user/show/19767615-henz">Henz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=sweet-guys">sweet-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=swoon-worthy">swoon-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=hot-guy-alert">hot-guy-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=laughed-out-loud">laughed-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=cute-couple">cute-couple</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498949108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17330949138316295478">Another <em>Friends-with-benefits</em> book that I liked, this story is one of those cliché, I've seen movies with the some plot either way I like it because it’s a guilty pleasure <em>chick-lit</em> that can also be a guilty pleasure <em>chick-flick</em> if adapted.<br/><br/>Meet <strong>Emma </strong>who wants to have a child badly but she doesn’t have a man with her to do that anymore when her fiancée died in an accident and since then she’s devastated to start a relationship so she wants to be clinically conceived and wants her gay friend’s see</span>
  <span id="freeText17330949138316295478" style="display:none">Another <em>Friends-with-benefits</em> book that I liked, this story is one of those cliché, I've seen movies with the some plot either way I like it because it’s a guilty pleasure <em>chick-lit</em> that can also be a guilty pleasure <em>chick-flick</em> if adapted.<br><br>Meet <strong>Emma </strong>who wants to have a child badly but she doesn’t have a man with her to do that anymore when her fiancée died in an accident and since then she’s devastated to start a relationship so she wants to be clinically conceived and wants her gay friend’s seeds that way she won’t risk spawning a serial killer but you see her friend backed out for the reason that his partner was against the idea.<br><br>Okay I was really cracking up reading this because I have a gay friend that propositioned something like this to another friend of mine so that he could have a child too. Guys these things are so normal! Just saying!<br><br>Then meet <strong>Aidan</strong> who is the <em>manwhore</em> (I know, I know … cliché but I don’t care!) he is sweet but has his moments of being an asshole. He likes Emma and since he knows about her dilemma.<br><br>He made a <em>proposition</em> to offer his seeds along with his excellent DNA (the way he brags it) only if she had to conceive it naturally … that means SEX right?! .. That’s where the fun begins!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452146147ra/17651812.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He did this because he hates commitments and it’s a chance of fulfilling his late mother’s wish of him having kids without being tied up in a relationship. The whole idea is like a business deal, and there a contract for Pete’s sake! But I get why it’s needed.<br><br>I swooned a lot in this book, I find the whole being pregnant thing adorable, it was enjoyable and fast paced and funny, I liked how the story developed, I was devastated at the ending but good thing there’s a book 2 to make up for that …<br><br>Warning though, it's a steamy romance .. *wink*</span>

<div id="review_907213146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907213146" />
    <a title="Mei" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6876967-mei"><img alt="Mei" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422277196p2/6876967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907213146?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mei" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mei" href="/user/show/6876967-mei">Mei</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6876967-mei?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6876967-mei?shelf=no-books">no-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907213146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5797845859336091510">I wanted a fluffy, funny, easy book, but instead I got a book that get on my nerves in a big way!!!<br/><br/>Let’s see…<br/><br/>Emma… beautiful, sweet, successful, wounded, insecure (when necessary), fantastic Emma. She’s so strong, she’s suffered so much… Poor Emma! <br/><br/>Pssstt.. can you hear my sarcasm here?<br/><br/>Since the very beginning, we get what Emma wants, needs…<br/><br/><b>
  <i> Being husbandless and childless was all the more painful after her parents’ deaths. After losing her mother two years ago, she had sworn she would replac</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText5797845859336091510" style="display:none">I wanted a fluffy, funny, easy book, but instead I got a book that get on my nerves in a big way!!!<br /><br />Let’s see…<br /><br />Emma… beautiful, sweet, successful, wounded, insecure (when necessary), fantastic Emma. She’s so strong, she’s suffered so much… Poor Emma! <br /><br />Pssstt.. can you hear my sarcasm here?<br /><br />Since the very beginning, we get what Emma wants, needs…<br /><br /><b>
  <i> Being husbandless and childless was all the more painful after her parents’ deaths. After losing her mother two years ago, she had sworn she would replace the love she had lost by finding a husband and having a child.</i>
</b><br /><br />That’s such a mature desire!!! Ohhhh, Emma has suffered sooooo much… poor her… I’m crying here!!!<br /><br />So what’s her wonderful, intelligent, clever idea??? She torment her gay friend to donate his sperm!! And she’s irked when he refuses!!! Oh, sweet Emma!!! <br /><br />Her friend Casey is not much better:<br /><b>
  <i> “You just need to tell him to man-up, grow a pair and give you some sperm.” .</i>
</b><br /><br />Ok, since Connor is such a bad person and doesn’t want to father her child, she accept Aidan “proposition” to have sex with him and get pregnant!!! Such a mature and intelligent thing!!!<br /><br />I can understand Aidan, he’s a man-whore and he’ll get a lot of sex. But Emma? She’s less than 30 years old, but her fertility clock is ticking??? What??? Nowdays 30 years old women are considered young. I’m feeling almost insulted on behalf of all the women who start planning children after their 30th birthday!<br /><br />Ok, I say to myself, this is chick-lit, erotic fiction, so you have to forgive some inaccuracies, but as I read on things get worse and worse…<br /><br />Emma, being such a sweet girl, makes a contract for Aidan to sign where she’s protecting herself and Aidan too. Ohhhh, such a wonderful way to be happy and complete after having suffered soooo much (see above)!!!<br /><br />And they get going at it!!! Aidan is such a callous womanizer that he books a honeymoon suite, rose petals, candles, champagne, strawberries… Such an awful, awful thing to do!!! <br /><br />And so they f*ck and, obviously she’s falling for him and he’s falling for her. That’s OK, this is chick-lit, erotic romance.<br /><br />But… Aidan constantly “complains” about Emma’s <i>mouth</i>. And not is <i>that</i> way! <br />She’s so clever and funny… Hmmm, here are some examples:<br /><br /><b>
  <i> “Of course. I mean, we can’t have anything happening to that fabulous ass of yours now can we?”<br />“That mouth of yours is trouble,”<br />--------------------------------<br />“I can’t believe Mr. Aidan Fitzgerald—Sex God Extraordinaire—is doubting his bedroom abilities.”<br />At her taunting, Aidan’s expressed flipped over from anxious to smoldering in barely a second.<br />“There goes that mouth of yours again,”<br />--------------------------------<br />“Of course, I<br />wasn’t an All State Swim Champion, so what do I know?”<br />Aidan shook his head as he threw off the quilt. “There goes that mouth of yours again.” .</i>
</b><br /><br />Am I the only one who doesn’t find anything fun there??? OK, maybe it is an American kind of humor that I don’t get…<br /><br />And I continued reading, hoping things will get better…<br /><br />So we get to know why Aidan is a womanizer. He’s a broken man. He’s wounded too. He’s aver 30, but he’s still suffering from abandonment when he was 20. Poor baby… He has been tricked and he reiterated by cheating. Sooo mature!<br /><br />But their falling in love goes on and more it goes on more I get annoyed by both of them, but mostly by Emma.<br /><br /><b>
  <i> Aidan’s voice came muffled from under the pillow. “Em, would you mind taking him and the screaming somewhere else?”<br />Rage burned through Emma. How dare he treat her that way? Shifting Mason onto her shoulder, she used her free hand to smack Aidan’s naked back. Hard. <br />He flung back the pillow and glared up at her. “What the hell was that for?”<br />“Why are you being such an insensitive asshole?”<br />“Because I’m overworked, jet-lagged, and just want to sleep,” he growled. <br />Emma shook her head. “Your behavior tonight is seriously giving me something to think about.”<br />Aidan rose up in the bed and rubbed his eyes. “What are you bitching about now?”<br />“Is this how it’s going to be with our baby? You only thinking of your own selfish needs, resenting the baby when it comes between us and sex, and most of all, making it seem like I’m a single parent when you’re in the same room with me?”<br />With a roll of his eyes, Aidan jerked off the sheet. “Fine. I’ll go fix his fucking bottle. Will that make you happy?”<br />“Maybe,” she replied. Even though he stomped bare-assed out of the room, Emma grinned that her speech had affected him enough to react. Every little battle was a victory in her favor. .</i>
</b><br /><br />Oh, how dare he treat her like that???! Bad, bad Aidan!!! <br /><br />Hey, Emma, I know that you’re in love with him, but he’s still just a sperm donor, not your insanely in love sweetheart!!! What did you expect? <br /><br />We know that Aidan is falling in love too, but he’s still fighting it. He’s so immature that’s incredible!<br /><br />All the characters in this book are so immature and sketchy at best. Emma, Aidan, Casey, Emma’s grandparents, Aidan’s family… They act like a stereotype characters: the BF, they loving grannies, the perfect siblings… It’s so saccharine that I almost got diabetes!<br /><br />And the ending? Yes, it does have a cliffhanger… of sorts…<br /><br />The strange thing that I’m reading the sequel!!! I must have some masochistic tenedencies!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5797845859336091510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_453499470" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453499470?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen">Kristen</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer453499470" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15470138310303695159"><b>DNF at 20%</b><br/><br/>I've put this book down for the time being. I'm having a very difficult time with Emma's over-the-top <b>need</b> to have a baby. The fact she feels her biological clock is "clanking" not just ticking at such a young age (she's not even 30 yet) is too much for me. For some reason, and I'm not sure why, I'm not emotionally able to move pass her desperate behavior and enjoy the rest of the story.<br/></span>

<div id="review_446881232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/446881232" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/446881232?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-erotica">genre-erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=new-authors-review">new-authors-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-contemp-romance">genre-contemp-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer446881232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6458657080192133476">When I read the blurb for this, I expected a fairly erotic little romance. And it was, for sure. But there was a lot more depth to it than I was prepared for. <br/><br/>The setup...the Proposition...takes place fairly quickly. Emma is an almost thirty year old woman with no romantic prospects. She's fairly successful financially. But she's alone in the world family wise, after her Mom passes away. She's also VERY innocent. Not virginal, but the woman has only slept with one man in her life, her fiancee, w</span>
  <span id="freeText6458657080192133476" style="display:none">When I read the blurb for this, I expected a fairly erotic little romance. And it was, for sure. But there was a lot more depth to it than I was prepared for. <br /><br />The setup...the Proposition...takes place fairly quickly. Emma is an almost thirty year old woman with no romantic prospects. She's fairly successful financially. But she's alone in the world family wise, after her Mom passes away. She's also VERY innocent. Not virginal, but the woman has only slept with one man in her life, her fiancee, who also died over four years ago. So she's not very experienced in matters of love or sex. But her intentions are honorable. She wants to be a Mom. She wants someone to live for, love beyond all reason...she wants someone who NEEDS her. And I can totally relate to that. I was so impressed with how the author made me empathize with Emma. I was hurting for her and that empty womb and those empty arms. <br /><br />Aiden has lusted after Emma since she spurned him at the company Christmas party. He's a big ole player, but I actually loved him! He's funny and sweet and quite the thoughtful man slut, actually. He doesn't try to decieve Emma into thinking that he wants anything more than to sleep with her. In fact, he makes it very clear that he will want nothing to do with the baby. This is a trade that they're making and when the deal is done, so is he. Emma, while nervous as hell, finally agrees to the trade off. Instead of a cold, sterile clinic for conception, she also gets to feel passion again...something she hasn't felt since the death of her fiancee. <br /><br />As I said earlier, I really liked Aiden! Though their setup is sort of clandestine, he tries to make it as good as possible for Emma. He's not a coldhearted player. Just a horny guy. And he knows how special this is for her. So what does Emma do? Yep, she starts to fall for him. This is where I started to get a wee bit frustrated with Emma. I mean, the rules are laid out...they even draw up a contract! (A la Fify Shades without the whips and chains, which Aiden alludes to and made me literally laugh out loud) So Emma just acts like such a <b>girl</b> in regards to their relationship. Her proprietary actions toward Aiden started to rub me the wrong way. He's not a bad guy, and she starts acting like he's doing bad things.<br /><br />To be quite honest, even I fell a little in love with Aiden. He's just such a great guy! And when one thing leads to another and they start spending more and more time together, we get to the heart of them both. We meet both of their families and begin to learn what makes both Emma and Aiden tick. Aiden, while professing to revel in his single status, has much more to him than what he shows the world. By no means is he perfect. He makes some pretty rockin' mistakes and there is a major point of contention that I see popping up with some readers. However, people make mistakes, and Aiden is about as redeemable a hero as I can imagine. <br /><br />If there is one thing that I would change, I would want more descriptive writing. While the point is always made, often I felt as if I needed juuuust a little more of the scene. The first time I noticed it was after a sex scene. They go from orgasm to post-coital chatting in one sentence. No heavy breathing or lightheaded come downs. Just 'Oh yes, Aiden!' and moving on.... After that, I started to notice how a lot of details were left out, things that, to me, could have pulled me into the scene and made it more real. It wasn't bad writing by any means, but I do think that I could have connected with the entire story as a whole if I'd felt more aware of the people, how they looked, sounded, felt, etc. Lots of dialogue, which I normally love, but I wanted to LOOK at Aiden while he was talking instead of just listening to him. If that makes sense.<br /><br />The end.....AAAAAAAAAAHHH!!!! I KNEW it was coming, I was warned from previous reviews. But I couldn't help myself. And I think being prepared for it was a good thing, because while I still cried and ranted, I could handle it. Had I NOT known...I'd have been hunting someone DOWN!!! Just kidding, not a stalker here. Let me just say that January can't possibly come fast enough!! I'm so very glad that this is a romance and I (hopefully) know how it all will end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6458657080192133476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7319146783214549470">Yeah, nope.<br/>*Spoilers ahead, btw*<br/><br/>So, let's see. <br/>We have a girl (can't get myself to call her woman) who is reaaaaly desperate to get a kid because her biological clock is ticking. She's not even 30 yet. But she's so old! It's not like most females these days have a kid when they're over 30, because that's just way too old!<br/><br/>Ok, let's say I'd overlook that part if she was a cool chick.   <span id="freeText7319146783214549470" style="display:none">Yeah, nope.<br />*Spoilers ahead, btw*<br /><br />So, let's see. <br />We have a girl (can't get myself to call her woman) who is reaaaaly desperate to get a kid because her biological clock is ticking. She's not even 30 yet. But she's so old! It's not like most females these days have a kid when they're over 30, because that's just way too old!<br /><br />Ok, let's say I'd overlook that part if she was a cool chick. But no luck there either. She's so damn needy and annoying and idiotic most of the times!<br /><br />She gets mad at her gay best friend because he doesn't want to give her his sperm. Like that's what any normal guy would do, just father a child because someone else wants that. <br /><br />She meets a co-worker at one point who so generously offers to have sex with her so that she can become a mum. Yup, another typical, normal, smart guy. Let's make a baby together, who cares what happens next with the kid!<br />*kids and irresponsible, idiotic parents are my weak point, in case you haven't noticed yet*<br /><br />God, and the way they talk and act! <br />People really should get an IQ test or something before they can have a kid.<br /><br />Anyway, I expected a nice, fun, relaxing story yet I got this. I just couldn't not DNF this book. I don't wanna waste any more of my time on this kinds of reads.<br /><br />If anyone actually got to this part of my review, I'm, as they say it, strongly advising you against reading this thing. Definitely not worth the (OMG!!!) over 4-stars rating.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442115650" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3622519588848707058"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395542i/761863._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395542i/761864._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What?! <b>Whaaaaat?!</b> You have got to be kidding me?! Ok, once again, my lack of research before diving, blind, into a book, gets the better of me. I did not know there was a second book and that this did not end in a HEA. And now I have to wait until March! <i>MARCH</i>!!! To find out what happens. Gah, torture!<br/><br/>However, that aside, I <i>loved</i> The Proposition. It was original, emotional, sweet, steamy, well paced, witty, fantastically written... just brilliant!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Is this one of those contracts like in that k</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3622519588848707058" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395542i/761863._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395542i/761864._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What?! <b>Whaaaaat?!</b> You have got to be kidding me?! Ok, once again, my lack of research before diving, blind, into a book, gets the better of me. I did not know there was a second book and that this did not end in a HEA. And now I have to wait until March! <i>MARCH</i>!!! To find out what happens. Gah, torture!<br><br>However, that aside, I <i>loved</i> The Proposition. It was original, emotional, sweet, steamy, well paced, witty, fantastically written... just brilliant!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Is this one of those contracts like in that kinky book where we outline what we're willing to do or not do during sex? Like our hard limits and safe words?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Emma was a great character. She knew what she wanted and she was determined to have it. She wasn't afraid of life or of hurt, despite having been through more than her share of heartache. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Have you ever wanted something so bad you think you’d die if you don’t have it? That the mere thought of it keeps you up at night. You can’t sleep, you can’t eat, you can’t drink. You are so consumed by that desire nothing else matters, and you’re not sure life is worth living if you can’t have it."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Aidan Fitzgerald I hate you! Oh but I love you! But right now I hate you! (And love you a little bit)! Aidan had moments of brilliance although I think I'd have kicked his ass into touch before now. He was super cute at times, very sexy but infuriatingly detached. But who can resist a man with a naughty, sexy mouth. The dialogue in this book is just great and had the butterflies in my stomach performing somersaults!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“How much plainer can I make it for you? You were so damn sexy in that green dress. Your hair was down and fell in waves around your shoulders. And you kept giving me those innocent little smiles from across the room. I’ve never wanted to fuck someone so much as I wanted to you.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The sex is fantastic! Katie Ashley can write the shit out of a sex scene and there are some seriously steamy parts to this book. I love how the relationship between Emma and Aidan develops. It doesn't feel forced or unnatural in any way. The book isn't particularly short but I felt like it flew by, the story really drew me in.<br><br>Absolutely can't wait for The Proposal. Now if you'll excuse me, I'm off to sulk until it is released.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15579181235863820271">Before you read this I want to say sorry in advance for the rant below. <br/><br/>If I had to use one word that would describe this book then it would have to be predictable or unrealistic. <br/><br/>First of all, if Aiden was really a player who never wants to be tied down, he would have never agree to have a child with a women he would have to see day in and day out at work!   <span id="freeText15579181235863820271" style="display:none">Before you read this I want to say sorry in advance for the rant below. <br /><br />If I had to use one word that would describe this book then it would have to be predictable or unrealistic. <br /><br />First of all, if Aiden was really a player who never wants to be tied down, he would have never agree to have a child with a women he would have to see day in and day out at work! That in itself would be to much of a commitment for him, because he would have to see her all the time, and in turn, ask about the baby. <br /><br />Secondly, the dialog in this book pissed me off. Unrealistic. It's like the author thought of a bunch of cleaver innuendos, some encounters she wanted to use and some banter and then threw them together without much thought. I feel bad saying that because I know how hard it is to write, but honestly this book got on my nerves. I wanted to tell the guy to be a man and I wanted to tell Emma to grow a lady pair and open her freaking eyes!<br /><br />If it wasn't for the fact that I rarely ever start a book without finishing it, I would have put this book down after the first three chapters. <br /><br />And to top it all off I have to read a squeal just because there is one and I will want it to be better than this one even though I know it won't be.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1235067397600787471">I'm going to start by saying I had high hopes for this book... And it exceeded my expectations! I loved it! Definitely my kind if read.<br/><br/>Emma is such a sweet lovable character. She has lost a lot of important people in her life the last few years, and with her biological clock ticking, she realizes she wants her own family and doesn't want to wait for the perfect timing or husband. Aidan... Well he is smoking hot, but also the known player of the office. He's got the hots for Emma, but after heari</span>
  <span id="freeText1235067397600787471" style="display:none">I'm going to start by saying I had high hopes for this book... And it exceeded my expectations! I loved it! Definitely my kind if read.<br /><br />Emma is such a sweet lovable character. She has lost a lot of important people in her life the last few years, and with her biological clock ticking, she realizes she wants her own family and doesn't want to wait for the perfect timing or husband. Aidan... Well he is smoking hot, but also the known player of the office. He's got the hots for Emma, but after hearing of his reputation she turns him down at the company Christmas party. Months later, he overhears Emma arguing with one of her best friends Conner about her situation. This gives Aidan an idea... He gives Emma a proposition that he thinks would work out perfectly for the both of them. He will be Emma's sperm donor, if the can conceive the baby the natural way... It's a win win, right???<br /><br />It is- until feelings and families get involved. I'm pretty sure it's safe to say Aidan has some pretty serious commitment issues. When he starts to develop feelings for Emma I think it really freaks him out. He doesn't know what to do and I really believe he doesn't want to hurt Emma or break her heart.<br /><br />Emma and Aidan were great together! There were some really HOT scenes too! Both Emma and Aidan were great mc's. Aidan wasn't perfect, but I loved him anyway! At least the first 90%... The last 10% I wanted to throw something at him! By the end of the book, I had really high hopes he could redeem himself, I can't wait to read the second book to find out if he does!<br /><br />This book was funny, frustrating, charming and sexy! There wasn't much about it I didn't love!!!</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206613-laura-carson?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206613-laura-carson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206613-laura-carson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206613-laura-carson?shelf=tbr-2012">tbr-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206613-laura-carson?shelf=pregnancy">pregnancy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206613-laura-carson?shelf=authors-to-watch">authors-to-watch</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer435278202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10653959018889468025">My dear Katie Ashley,<br/> I ask with love, what the f*ck was that? I'm a little angry at you for the ending, but if I'm being honest I'm really still angry with Aidan. I don't know how I'm going to wait till March! Anyhow, let's talk about this book of yours I just finished....<br/>Holy hell I feel like my heart aches and my gut is just now settling down. Emotions. A good book is one that makes you experience many of them from laughing out loud to gut wrenching sadness and dissapointment. I experienced t</span>
  <span id="freeText10653959018889468025" style="display:none">My dear Katie Ashley,<br /> I ask with love, what the f*ck was that? I'm a little angry at you for the ending, but if I'm being honest I'm really still angry with Aidan. I don't know how I'm going to wait till March! Anyhow, let's talk about this book of yours I just finished....<br />Holy hell I feel like my heart aches and my gut is just now settling down. Emotions. A good book is one that makes you experience many of them from laughing out loud to gut wrenching sadness and dissapointment. I experienced them all from start to finish with this one. Aidan &amp; Emma are very realistic characters. I cheered for them the entire time. Even when Aidan clearly had his head up his ass. Emma is a little nieve but it's a nice contrast to Adain. The story starts out a little choppy but progressivley gets smoother as it continues. The sex also improves as the book continues. In the beginning it felt mechanical. As the chemistry between the characters progresses I think it helps to improve it dramatically. <br /><br />There is something else I wanted to address in this review that gets personal. I have heard people say that Emma's desire to have a child, and the way she reacts when she doesn't get pregnant right away is unrealistic and childish. While I completley understand their thinking and have no disrespect for their opinions, I want to say that I actually understood her feelings. Yes, it's not fair to expect to get pregnant right away, and some struggle much longer, while some never succeed. However, I think the author captured her feelings perfectly. I personaly have experienced the gut wrenching jealousy(no matter how guilty or wrong I felt about those feelings) towards friends that were pregnant before I had my son. I also have a best friend in the same boat as Emma and just wishes for a baby, no matter that she hasn't met that special man yet(and has joked about doing the same thing. And is 27, a little younger than Emma). It's insane the level of resentment you feel at times, and the heartbreak every month when you get your hopes up only to have them shot down when it's negative. Again, I think the author captured her feelings perfectly, IMO. Not saying everyone feels the same way, but I think it's a valid perspective for some woman who find themselves not in the place they thought they would be.<br />*getting off my soapbox now*<br />So I say in all sincerity...all in all I think this series has so much potential, and even with a rocky start, ended up leaving me wanting more. Looking forward to book #2!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10653959018889468025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EoX4IW7CLxB556/ijUVM/SsIBAfKT2XUn557UgA3U5cJTwvSqkq6SV+UYJ61rGdehM4C+iDEZqcEJkb4v3/uKw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('llSvG5gPJhkrAsTDSKawb0CgD9QAFqXwzV8oTkVQaWWNnlzoXIezQA1xC79wT5vM72YJKeqdpoNW5xXk+hjU2Q==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText4777521909719156054" style="display:none">Katie Ashley is a New York Times, USA Today, and Amazon Top Three Best-Selling author of both Indie and Traditionally published books. She's written rockers, bikers, manwhores with hearts of gold, New Adult, and Young Adult. She has a slight obsession with The Golden Girls, Shakespeare, Harry Potter, and Star Wars. <br /><br />With a BA in English, a BS in Secondary English Education, and a Masters in Adolescent English Education, she spent eleven years teaching both middle and high school English, as well as a few adjunct college English classes. As of January 2013, she became a full-time writer.<br /><br />Although she is a life-long Georgia peach, she loves traveling the country and world meeting readers. This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
